     <p>
      <i>
       <b>
        Monty Python's Spamalot
       </b>
      </i>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">
       musical comedy
      </a>
      adapted from the 1975 film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python_and_the_Holy_Grail" title="Monty Python and the Holy Grail">
        Monty Python and the Holy Grail
       </a>
      </i>
      . Like the film, it is a highly irreverent parody of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arthurian_Legend" title="Arthurian Legend">
       Arthurian Legend
      </a>
      , but it differs from the film in many ways.
     </p>
     <p>
      One of the musical's creators, Eric Idle, explained the title in a February 2004 press release:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       I like the title
       <i>
        Spamalot
       </i>
       a lot. We tested it with audiences on my recent US tour and they liked it as much as I did, which is gratifying. After all, they are the ones who will be paying Broadway prices to see the show. It comes from a line in the movie which goes: "we eat ham, and jam, and
       <a href="/wiki/Spam_(Monty_Python)" title="Spam (Monty Python)">
        Spam
       </a>
       a lot."
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      The original 2005 Broadway production, directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Mike_Nichols" title="Mike Nichols">
       Mike Nichols
      </a>
      , won three
      <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">
       Tony Awards
      </a>
      , including the
      <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Musical">
       Tony Award for Best Musical
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/59th_Tony_Awards" title="59th Tony Awards">
       20042005 season
      </a>
      and received 14 Tony Award nominations. During its initial run of over 1,500 performances it was seen by more than two million people and grossed over $175 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playbillend_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-playbillend-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39">
        <a href="#Awards_and_nominations">
         <span class="tocnumber">

         </span>

         </span>
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40">

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">
       Synopsis
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Synopsis">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div style="width:52px">
         <img alt="Globe icon." data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" width="48"/>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         The examples and perspective in this article
         <b>
          may not represent a
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">
           worldwide view
          </a>
          of the subject
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Please
          <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit">
           improve this article
          </a>
          and discuss the issue on the
          <a href="/wiki/Talk:Spamalot" title="Talk:Spamalot">
           talk page
          </a>
          .
         </span>
         <small>
          <i>
           (December 2010)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Before_the_Musical">
       Before the Musical
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Before the Musical">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A recording encourages members of the audience to "let your cellphones and pagers ring willy-nilly," and comments that they should "be aware there are heavily armed knights on stage that may drag you on stage and impale you." This was recorded by John Cleese.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Act_I">
       Act I
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Act I">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A historian gives a brief overview of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval" title="Medieval">
       medieval
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">
       England
      </a>
      . In a miscommunication between the actors and the narrator, a Scandinavian village appears, with Finnish villagers along with the Mayor of the country on his fort singing the "Fisch Schlapping Song." Ten men grab tiny fish and lightly slap the women in the face with them. After a couple of slaps, the women pull out much larger fish and slap the men in return with great force, making the men fall flat on the floor. The villagers continue to sing and dance. Then, two women slap the mayor hard in the face with enormous fish, both having huge smiles on their faces while slapping him. Because both women slapped him at the same time with so much force, the mayor falls flat on the floor, then leaves the stage. His fort is then taken over by one of the women who slapped him. The villagers continue to sing and dance. The Historian returns, irritated, and tells the frolicking Finns that he was talking about
      <b>
       Eng
      </b>
      land, not
      <b>
       Fin
      </b>
      land. The scene immediately goes to a dreary, dark village with penitent
      <a href="/wiki/Monk" title="Monk">
       monks
      </a>
      in hooded robes chanting
      <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
       Latin
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/King_Arthur" title="King Arthur">
       King Arthur
      </a>
      travels the land with his servant Patsy, who follows him around banging two coconut shells together to make the sound of a horse's hooves as Arthur "rides" before him, trying to recruit
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knights_of_the_Round_Table" title="Knights of the Round Table">
       Knights of the Round Table
      </a>
      to join him in
      <a href="/wiki/Camelot" title="Camelot">
       Camelot
      </a>
      . He encounters a pair of sentries who are more interested in debating whether two swallows could successfully carry a coconut than in listening to the king.
     </p>
     <p>
      Sir Robin, a collector of
      <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">
       plague
      </a>
      victims, and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Lancelot" title="Sir Lancelot">
       Lancelot
      </a>
      , a large, handsome and incredibly violent man, meet as Lancelot attempts to dispose of the sickly Not Dead Fred
      <i>
       ("He Is Not Dead Yet")
      </i>
      . They agree to become Knights of the Round Table together, Lancelot for the fighting, and Robin for the singing and the dancing.
     </p>
     <p>
      Arthur attempts to convince a peasant named Dennis Galahad that he, Arthur, is king of England because the
      <a href="/wiki/Lady_of_the_Lake" title="Lady of the Lake">
       Lady of the Lake
      </a>
      gave him
      <a href="/wiki/Excalibur" title="Excalibur">
       Excalibur
      </a>
      , the sword given only to the man fit to rule England. However, Dennis and his mother, Mrs Galahad, are
      <a href="/wiki/Political_radicalism" title="Political radicalism">
       political radicals
      </a>
      and deny that any king who has not been elected by the people has any legitimate right to rule over them. To settle the issue, Arthur has the Lady Of The Lake and her Laker Girls appear to turn Dennis into a knight
      <i>
       ("Come With Me")
      </i>
      . Cheered on by the girls
      <i>
       ("Laker Girls Cheer")
      </i>
      , the Lady Of The Lake turns Dennis into
      <a href="/wiki/Galahad" title="Galahad">
       Sir Galahad
      </a>
      and together, they sing a generic Broadway love song
      <i>
       ("
       <a href="/wiki/The_Song_That_Goes_Like_This" title="The Song That Goes Like This">
        The Song That Goes Like This
       </a>
       ")
      </i>
      , complete with chandelier. They are joined by Sir Robin and Sir Lancelot, and together with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bedevere" title="Bedevere">
       Sir Bedevere
      </a>
      and "the aptly named" Sir Not-Appearing-In-This-Show (a knight resembling
      <a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">
       Don Quixote
      </a>
      , who promptly apologises and leaves), they make up the Knights of the Round Table
      <i>
       ("All For One")
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The five knights gather in
      <a href="/wiki/Camelot" title="Camelot">
       Camelot
      </a>
      , a deliberately anachronistic place resembling
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">
       Las Vegas's
      </a>
      Camelot-inspired
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Excalibur_Hotel" title="Excalibur Hotel">
       Excalibur resort
      </a>
      , complete with showgirls, oversized dice and the Lady of the Lake headlining the Castle in full
      <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">
       Cher
      </a>
      get-up
      <i>
       ("Knights Of The Round Table"/"The Song That Goes Like This (Reprise)")
      </i>
      . In the midst of their revelry, they are contacted by
      <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">
       God
      </a>
      (a recording voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/John_Cleese" title="John Cleese">
       John Cleese
      </a>
      of the original Monty Python troupe and Eric Idle in the version currently touring the UK) who tells them to locate the
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_Grail" title="Holy Grail">
       Holy Grail
      </a>
      . Urged on by the Lady Of The Lake
      <i>
       ("Find Your Grail")
      </i>
      , the Knights set off. They travel throughout the land until they reach a castle, only to be viciously taunted by lewd
      <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">
       French
      </a>
      soldiers. They attempt to retaliate by sending them a large wooden rabbit in the style of the
      <a href="/wiki/Trojan_Horse" title="Trojan Horse">
       Trojan Horse
      </a>
      ; however, they realise after the fact that it was not as simple as leaving the rabbit and walking away  they should have hidden inside it. Defeated, they leave in a hurry when the French begin taunting them again, sending
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cancan" title="Cancan">
       cancan
      </a>
      dancers after them and throwing barnyard animals including cows at them
      <i>
       ("Run Away!")
      </i>
      . Arthur and his followers manage to run into the safety of the wings before the French catapult the Trojan Rabbit at them.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Act_II">
       Act II
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Act II">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Sir Robin and his minstrels follow King Arthur and Patsy into a "dark and very expensive forest", where they are separated. King Arthur meets the terrifying but silly
      <a href="/wiki/Knights_who_say_Ni" title="Knights who say Ni">
       Knights who say Ni
      </a>
      , who demand a
      <a href="/wiki/Shrubbery" title="Shrubbery">
       shrubbery
      </a>
      . King Arthur despairs of finding one, but Patsy cheers him up
      <i>
       ("
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Always_Look_On_The_Bright_Side_Of_Life" title="Always Look On The Bright Side Of Life">
        Always Look On The Bright Side Of Life
       </a>
       ")
      </i>
      and they find a shrubbery shortly after.
     </p>
     <p>
      Sir Robin, after wandering the forest for some time with his minstrels
      <i>
       ("Brave Sir Robin")
      </i>
      , encounters
      <a href="/wiki/Black_Knight_(Monty_Python)" title="Black Knight (Monty Python)">
       The Black Knight
      </a>
      , who scares him off, but King Arthur, who happens on the scene, more or less defeats him by cutting off both his arms and legs, impaling his still-alive torso on a door, and leaving to give the Knights their shrubbery. The Knights accept it, but next demand that King Arthur put on a musical and bring it to Broadway (in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      , this became a
      <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">
       West End
      </a>
      musical; on the tour, they must put on a "Broadway musical"), implying that it need only be Broadway-style, "but not an
      <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lloyd_Webber" title="Andrew Lloyd Webber">
       Andrew Lloyd Webber
      </a>
      ". The mere mention of his name causes everyone to cover their ears and scream in pain. Sir Robin, who has found Arthur by this point, insists that it would be impossible for them to accomplish this next task, since you need
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jew" title="Jew">
       Jews
      </a>
      for a successful Broadway (or West End) musical
      <i>
       ("You Won't Succeed On Broadway")
      </i>
      , and proves his point in a wild production number filled with
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Fiddler_on_the_Roof" title="Fiddler on the Roof">
        Fiddler on the Roof
       </a>
      </i>
      parodies, including a bottle dance like the one in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiddler_On_The_Roof" title="Fiddler On The Roof">
       Fiddler On The Roof
      </a>
      , with Grails instead of bottles. King Arthur and Patsy promptly set off in search of Jews.
     </p>
     <p>
      (In countries that don't have a tradition of Jews in the theatre, the lyrics of
      <i>
       "You Won't Succeed on Broadway"
      </i>
      are sometimes changed to instead describe the high production standards and acting talent needed to stage a successful musical in that country. For example, in the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">
       South Korean
      </a>
      version, Sir Robin sings about recent successful musicals that were staged in
      <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">
       Seoul
      </a>
      during the previous decade. Meanwhile, members of the ensemble appear onstage dressed as various characters from those musicals. Among these characters are a cat from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Cats_(musical)" title="Cats (musical)">
        Cats
       </a>
      </i>
      , Kenickie from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Grease_(musical)" title="Grease (musical)">
        Grease
       </a>
      </i>
      , Kim from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Miss_Saigon" title="Miss Saigon">
        Miss Saigon
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Erik_(The_Phantom_of_the_Opera)" title="Erik (The Phantom of the Opera)">
       The Phantom
      </a>
      from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (1986 musical)">
        The Phantom of the Opera
       </a>
      </i>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Velma_Kelly" title="Velma Kelly">
       Velma Kelly
      </a>
      from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago_(musical)" title="Chicago (musical)">
        Chicago
       </a>
      </i>
      . As with the original version of the song, Sir Robin and the entire ensemble end the number with a song and dance routine.)
     </p>
     <p>
      While the Lady Of The Lake laments her lack of stage time
      <i>
       ("Whatever Happened To My Part?")
      </i>
      , Sir Lancelot receives a letter from what he assumes is a young damsel in distress. He is very surprised to find that the "damsel" is actually an embarrassingly effeminate young man named Prince Herbert
      <i>
       ("Where Are You?"/"Here Are You")
      </i>
      whose overbearing, music-hating father, the King of Swamp Castle, is forcing him into an arranged marriage. As Herbert is asking Lancelot to help him escape, the King of Swamp Castle cuts the rope that he is using to climb out of the window, and Herbert falls to his apparent death. Lancelot is a bit puzzled at the king's actions, but it is revealed that Herbert was saved at the last minute by Lancelot's sidekick, Concorde. The King asks his son how he was saved, exactly, to which Herbert replies happily with a song. But the king charges at his son with a spear, preparing to kill him. Lancelot steps in to save him, then gives a tearful, heartfelt speech about sensitivity to the king on Herbert's behalf, and Lancelot is
      <a href="/wiki/Outing" title="Outing">
       outed
      </a>
      as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homosexual" title="Homosexual">
       homosexual
      </a>
      in the process, an announcement celebrated in a wild disco number
      <i>
       ("His Name is Lancelot")
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      King Arthur begins to give up hope of ever putting on the Broadway musical and laments that he is alone, even though Patsy has been with him the entire time
      <i>
       ("I'm All Alone")
      </i>
      . The Lady Of The Lake appears and tells Arthur that he and the Knights have been in a Broadway musical all along. Patsy also reveals he is half Jewish, but didn't want to say anything to Arthur because "that's not really the sort of thing you say to a heavily armed
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christian
      </a>
      ." All that's left is for King Arthur to find the Grail and marry someone. After picking up on some not-too-subtle hints, Arthur decides to marry the Lady Of The Lake after he finds the Grail
      <i>
       ("Twice in Every Show")
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Reunited with his Knights, Arthur meets Tim the Enchanter who warns them of the danger of a
      <a href="/wiki/Rabbit_of_Caerbannog" title="Rabbit of Caerbannog">
       killer rabbit
      </a>
      . When the rabbit bites a knight's head off, Arthur uses the Holy Hand Grenade of Antioch against it, knocking down a nearby hill and revealing that the "evil rabbit" was actually a puppet controlled by a surprised puppeteer. A large stone block showing a combination of letters and numbers is also revealed. (The letters are based on the seat numbering system used by each theatre. They are changed from performance to performance to discourage audience members from intentionally booking any of the possible seats. The seat is typically on the aisle in one of the first few rows nearest the orchestra. In the Broadway production and on the tour it is either A101, B101, C101 or D101; i.e., Seat 101  which is
      <a href="/wiki/Blocking_(stage)" title="Blocking (stage)">
       house right
      </a>
      of the center aisle  of Rows A, B, C, or D.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the West End Production a word is revealed  DONE, CONE or BONE, referring to D1, C1 and B1 respectively.) After pondering the final clue, Arthur admits that they're "a bit stumped with the clue thing" and asks God to "give them a hand". A large hand points to the audience and Arthur realises that the letters and numbers refer to a seat number in the audience. The grail is "found" (with some sleight of hand) under the seat and the person sitting in the seat is rewarded with a small trophy and a
      <a href="/wiki/Instant_camera" title="Instant camera">
       polaroid
      </a>
      photo.
      <i>
       ("The Holy Grail")
      </i>
      . Arthur marries the Lady of the Lake, who reveals that her name is
      <a href="/wiki/Guinevere" title="Guinevere">
       Guinevere
      </a>
      ; Lancelot marries Herbert (who finally has a chance to sing); and Sir Robin decides to pursue a career in
      <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">
       musical theatre
      </a>
      <i>
       ("Act 2 Finale/Always Look on the Bright Side of Life (Company Bow)")
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The overall duration of the show is about two hours plus interval time.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_numbers">
       Musical numbers
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Musical numbers">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Eric Idle wrote the musical's
      <a href="/wiki/Libretto" title="Libretto">
       book and lyrics
      </a>
      and collaborated with
      <a href="/wiki/John_Du_Prez" title="John Du Prez">
       John Du Prez
      </a>
      on the music, except for "Knights of the Round Table" and "Brave Sir Robin", which were composed by
      <a href="/wiki/Neil_Innes" title="Neil Innes">
       Neil Innes
      </a>
      for
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python_and_the_Holy_Grail" title="Monty Python and the Holy Grail">
        Monty Python and the Holy Grail
       </a>
      </i>
      . ("Always Look on the Bright Side of Life" was originally written by Idle for the film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_Life_of_Brian" title="Monty Python's Life of Brian">
        Monty Python's Life of Brian
       </a>
      </i>
      .)
     </p>
     <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
      <tr>
       <td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
        <dl>
         <dt>
          Act I
         </dt>
        </dl>
        <ul>
         <li>
          Tuning**
         </li>
         <li>
          Overture
         </li>
         <li>
          "Historian's Introduction to Act I"  Historian
         </li>
         <li>
          "Finland" / "
          <a href="/wiki/The_Fish-Slapping_Dance" title="The Fish-Slapping Dance">
           Fisch Schlapping Dance
          </a>
          "  Mayor and Company
         </li>
         <li>
          "Monk's Chant"  Company
         </li>
         <li>
          "King Arthur's Song"  King Arthur, Patsy*
         </li>
         <li>
          "I Am Not Dead Yet"  Not Dead Fred, Lance, Robin, and Bodies
         </li>
         <li>
          "Come with Me"  King Arthur, Lady of the Lake, and Laker girls
         </li>
         <li>
          "Laker Girls Cheer"  Laker Girls
         </li>
         <li>
          "
          <a href="/wiki/The_Song_That_Goes_Like_This" title="The Song That Goes Like This">
           The Song That Goes Like This
          </a>
          "  Sir Galahad and Lady of the Lake
         </li>
         <li>

         </li>

         </li>
         <li>
          "The Song That Goes Like This" (Reprise)  Lady of the Lake
         </li>
         <li>
          "Find Your Grail"  Lady Of The Lake and Company
         </li>
         <li>
          "Run Away!"  Company
         </li>
         <li>
          The Intermission**
         </li>
        </ul>
       </td>
       <td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
        <dl>
         <dt>
          Act II
         </dt>
        </dl>
        <ul>
         <li>
          "Historian's Introduction to Act II"  Historian
         </li>
         <li>
          "
          <a href="/wiki/Always_Look_on_the_Bright_Side_of_Life" title="Always Look on the Bright Side of Life">
           Always Look on the Bright Side of Life
          </a>
          "  Patsy, King Arthur, Knights, and Knights of Ni
         </li>
         <li>
          "Brave Sir Robin"  Sir Robin and Minstrels
         </li>
         <li>
          "You Won't Succeed on Broadway"  Sir Robin and Ensemble
         </li>
         <li>
          "Whatever Happened to My Part?"  Lady Of The Lake
         </li>
         <li>
          "Where Are You?"  Prince Herbert
         </li>
         <li>
          "Here Are You"  Prince Herbert
         </li>
         <li>
          "His Name is Lancelot"  Sir Lancelot, Prince Herbert, and Ensemble
         </li>
         <li>
          "I'm All Alone"  King Arthur, Patsy, and Knights
         </li>
         <li>
          "Twice in Every Show"  Lady Of The Lake and King Arthur
         </li>
         <li>
          "Act II Finale: I Am Not Dead Yet (Reprise) / Find Your Grail (Reprise) / The Song That Goes Like This (Reprise II)"  Company
         </li>
         <li>
          "Bows: Always Look on the Bright Side of Life (Reprise)"  Company and Audience
         </li>
        </ul>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      *Does not appear on the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Original_cast_album" title="Original cast album">
       Original cast album
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      **On the cast album but not in the show itself.
     </p>
     <p>
      The song 'You Won't Succeed On Broadway' was changed to the 'Star Song' in the UK tour.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Characters">
       Characters
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

       </span>

       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Court_of_Camelot">
       The Court of Camelot
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Court of Camelot">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
      <tr>
       <td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          King Arthur of Britain
         </li>
         <li>
          Sir Lancelot the Homicidally Brave
         </li>
         <li>
          Sir Robin, the Not-Quite-So-Brave-as-Sir-Lancelot
         </li>
         <li>

         </li>

         </li>
        </ul>
       </td>
       <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Patsy_(Monty_Python)" title="Patsy (Monty Python)">

          </a>
          : King Arthur's trusty servant/steed and constant companion.
         </li>

         </li>

         </li>

          </a>
          .
         </li>
        </ul>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_characters">
       Other characters
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other characters">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
      <tr>
       <td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          The Lady of the Lake
         </li>
         <li>
          Not Dead Fred
         </li>
         <li>
          Robin's Lead Minstrel
         </li>
         <li>
          The King of Swamp Castle (aka Herbert's Father)
         </li>
         <li>
          Prince Herbert
         </li>
         <li>
          French Taunter
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Black_Knight_(Monty_Python)" title="Black Knight (Monty Python)">
           The Black Knight
          </a>
          : A psychotic, "invincible" knight who will insist on fighting even after all his limbs have been cut off.
         </li>
         <li>
          The Head Knight who says "Ni!": The very tall leader of the most feared cult in the land: the dreaded
          <a href="/wiki/Knights_who_say_Ni" title="Knights who say Ni">
           Knights who say Ni
          </a>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          Tim the Enchanter
         </li>
         <li>
          Mrs. Galahad
         </li>
        </ul>
       </td>
       <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          The Killer
          <a href="/wiki/Rabbit_of_Caerbannog" title="Rabbit of Caerbannog">
           Rabbit of Caerbannog
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          Swamp Castle Guards
         </li>
         <li>
          Two Sentries
         </li>
         <li>
          Historian: the Narrator.
         </li>
         <li>
          The Laker Girls: The Lady of the Lake's backup dancers/cheerleaders.
         </li>
         <li>
          Knights of the Round Table
         </li>
         <li>
          Robins Minstrels
         </li>
         <li>
          God
         </li>
         <li>
          Holder of the Holy Grail: Whoever happens to be sitting in a certain seat at that performance.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      In tribute to the film, where six actors played the majority of the male parts (and a few female ones), several actors play multiple roles; the only major characters not doubling are Arthur and the Lady of the Lake. In the Broadway production, the following doubling is used:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Lancelot/2nd Sentry/The French Taunter/Knight of Ni/Tim the Enchanter
      </li>
      <li>
       Robin/1st Sentry/Brother Maynard/2nd Guard
      </li>
      <li>
       Galahad/King of Swamp Castle/Black Knight
      </li>
      <li>
       Patsy/Mayor of
       <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">
        Finland
       </a>
       /1st Guard
      </li>
      <li>
       Bedevere/Mrs. Galahad/Concorde
      </li>
      <li>
       The Historian/Prince Herbert/Not Dead Fred/Lead Minstrel/The French Taunter's Best Friend
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Sara Ramirez was intended to double as a witch but this part was cut from the final script.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Several pairs of characters originally played by the same Monty Python member were reduced to one: the Dead Collector and Sir Robin (Idle), the Large Man with a Dead Body and Sir Lancelot (Cleese), and Dennis the Politically-Active Peasant and Sir Galahad (
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Palin" title="Michael Palin">
       Michael Palin
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Production_history">
       Production history
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Production history">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Chicago">
       Chicago
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Chicago">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpamALotTicket.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="281" data-file-width="803" height="77" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SpamALotTicket.png/220px-SpamALotTicket.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SpamALotTicket.png/330px-SpamALotTicket.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SpamALotTicket.png/440px-SpamALotTicket.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SpamALotTicket.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A ticket from the first preview show
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Previews of the show began in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" title="Chicago, Illinois">
       Chicago
      </a>
      's Shubert Theatre (now the
      <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Theatre" title="Bank of America Theatre">
       Bank of America Theatre
      </a>
      ) on 21 December 2004; the show officially opened there on 9 January 2005.
     </p>
     <p>
      Two musical numbers were dropped from Act One while the production was still in Chicago.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      During the scene set in the "Witch Village", the
      <a href="/wiki/Torch_song" title="Torch song">
       torch song
      </a>
      "Burn Her!" was originally performed by Sir Bedevere, The Witch, Sir Robin, Lancelot and Villagers. At the French Castle, "The Cow Song", in a parody of a stereotypical
      <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">
       film noir
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Cabaret" title="Cabaret">
       cabaret
      </a>
      style, was performed by The Cow and French Citizens. Before the two songs were cut in Chicago, the lead vocals in both songs were sung by
      <a href="/wiki/Sara_Ramirez" title="Sara Ramirez">
       Sara Ramirez
      </a>
      . This gave her six songs in Act One, but no further appearances until scene five in Act Two, for "The Diva's Lament".
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Broadway">
       Broadway
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Broadway">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The musical previewed on
      <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">
       Broadway
      </a>
      , at
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
       New York
      </a>
      's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shubert_Theatre_(Broadway)" title="Shubert Theatre (Broadway)">
       Shubert Theatre
      </a>
      , beginning 14 February 2005, and, after some changes, officially opened on 17 March 2005.
      <a href="/wiki/Mike_Nichols" title="Mike Nichols">
       Mike Nichols
      </a>
      directed, and
      <a href="/wiki/Casey_Nicholaw" title="Casey Nicholaw">
       Casey Nicholaw
      </a>
      choreographed. The production won the
      <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Musical">
       Tony Award for Best Musical
      </a>
      and was nominated for 14 Tony Awards. The show played its final performance on 11 January 2009 after 35 previews and 1,575 performances; it was seen by more than two million people and grossed over $175 million, recouping its initial production costs in under six months.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playbillend_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-playbillend-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The original Broadway cast included
      <a href="/wiki/Tim_Curry" title="Tim Curry">
       Tim Curry
      </a>
      as King Arthur,
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_McGrath_(actor)" title="Michael McGrath (actor)">
       Michael McGrath
      </a>
      as Patsy,
      <a href="/wiki/David_Hyde_Pierce" title="David Hyde Pierce">
       David Hyde Pierce
      </a>
      as Sir Robin,
      <a href="/wiki/Hank_Azaria" title="Hank Azaria">
       Hank Azaria
      </a>
      as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Lancelot" title="Sir Lancelot">
       Sir Lancelot
      </a>
      and other roles (e.g., the French Taunter,
      <a href="/wiki/Knights_who_say_Ni" title="Knights who say Ni">
       Knight of Ni
      </a>
      , and Tim the Enchanter),
      <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Sieber" title="Christopher Sieber">
       Christopher Sieber
      </a>
      as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Galahad" title="Sir Galahad">
       Sir Galahad
      </a>
      and other roles (e.g., the Black Knight and Prince Herbert's Father), and
      <a href="/wiki/Sara_Ramirez" title="Sara Ramirez">
       Sara Ramirez
      </a>
      as the
      <a href="/wiki/Lady_of_the_Lake" title="Lady of the Lake">
       Lady of the Lake
      </a>
      . It also included
      <a href="/wiki/Christian_Borle" title="Christian Borle">
       Christian Borle
      </a>
      as Prince Herbert and other roles (e.g., the Historian and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Not_Dead_Fred" title="Not Dead Fred">
       Not Dead Fred
      </a>
      ), Steve Rosen as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Bedevere" title="Sir Bedevere">
       Sir Bedevere
      </a>
      and other roles (e.g., Concorde and Dennis's Mother) and
      <a href="/wiki/John_Cleese" title="John Cleese">
       John Cleese
      </a>
      as the (recorded) Voice of God.
     </p>
     <p>
      Notable cast replacements included:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Hank Azaria was replaced by
       <a href="/wiki/Steve_Kazee" title="Steve Kazee">
        Steve Kazee
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Tudyk" title="Alan Tudyk">
        Alan Tudyk
       </a>
       and later by
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Holmes_(actor)" title="Richard Holmes (actor)">
        Rick Holmes
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Sara Ramirez was replaced by
       <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Kennedy" title="Lauren Kennedy">
        Lauren Kennedy
       </a>
       , then by
       <a href="/wiki/Marin_Mazzie" title="Marin Mazzie">
        Marin Mazzie
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Waddingham" title="Hannah Waddingham">
        Hannah Waddingham
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Merle_Dandridge" title="Merle Dandridge">
        Merle Dandridge
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Tim Curry was replaced by
       <a href="/wiki/Simon_Russell_Beale" title="Simon Russell Beale">
        Simon Russell Beale
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Harry_Groener" title="Harry Groener">
        Harry Groener
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Hadary" title="Jonathan Hadary">
        Jonathan Hadary
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_Collins_(actor)" title="Stephen Collins (actor)">
        Stephen Collins
       </a>
       , Michael Siberry, and
       <a href="/wiki/John_O%27Hurley" title="John O'Hurley">
        John O'Hurley
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Christopher Sieber was replaced by
       <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Cleale" title="Lewis Cleale">
        Lewis Cleale
       </a>
       , then by
       <a href="/wiki/Bradley_Dean" title="Bradley Dean">
        Bradley Dean
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Christian Borle was replaced by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tom_Deckman_(actor)" title="Tom Deckman (actor)">
        Tom Deckman
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       David Hyde Pierce was replaced by Martin Moran,
       <a href="/wiki/Clay_Aiken" title="Clay Aiken">
        Clay Aiken
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Petkoff" title="Robert Petkoff">
        Robert Petkoff
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Michael McGrath was replaced by David Hibbard, then by
       <a href="/wiki/Drew_Lachey" title="Drew Lachey">
        Drew Lachey
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Steve Rosen was replaced by Jeffrey Kuhn, Brad Oscar and Wally Dunn.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="US_Tour">
       US Tour
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: US Tour">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       First National tour (20062009)
      </dt>
     </dl>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Natl_Theatre_Washington.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1121" data-file-width="1503" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Natl_Theatre_Washington.JPG/200px-Natl_Theatre_Washington.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Natl_Theatre_Washington.JPG/300px-Natl_Theatre_Washington.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Natl_Theatre_Washington.JPG/400px-Natl_Theatre_Washington.JPG 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Natl_Theatre_Washington.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         Spamalot'
        </i>
        s North American tour took it to Washington, D.C.'s
        <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="National Theatre (Washington, D.C.)">
         National Theatre
        </a>
        in May 2006.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A
      <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
       North American
      </a>
      tour commenced in spring 2006, and the cast included
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Siberry" title="Michael Siberry">
       Michael Siberry
      </a>
      as King Arthur,
      <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Dumas" title="Jeff Dumas">
       Jeff Dumas
      </a>
      as Patsy/Mayor/Guard, David Turner as Robin/Guard/Brother Maynard, Rick Holmes as Lancelot/French Taunter/Knight of Ni/Tim The Enchanter, Bradley Dean as Galahad/Black Knight/Herbert's Father, Tom Deckman as The Historian/Not Dead Fred/French Guard/Minstrel/Prince Herbert, Christopher Gurr as Sir Bedevere/Dennis's Mother/Concorde, and Pia Glenn (who remains slated for productions as late as June 2008)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Popejoy1_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Popejoy1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as the Lady of the Lake. Deckman moved to the Broadway production in November 2006 and was replaced by Christopher Sutton.
     </p>
     <p>
      The tour won three 2007
      <a href="/wiki/Touring_Broadway_Awards" title="Touring Broadway Awards">
       Touring Broadway Awards
      </a>
      , including Best New Musical.
     </p>
     <p>
      This same tour returned to
      <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
       Chicago
      </a>
      on 20 January 2009 at the Auditorium Theatre of
      <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_University" title="Roosevelt University">
       Roosevelt University
      </a>
      , this time with
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Chamberlain" title="Richard Chamberlain">
       Richard Chamberlain
      </a>
      as King Arthur.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This production costs $419,099.53 in artist fees/royalties for 8 performances in a venue in Florida.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Tour continued through the summer 2009, with dates at the
      <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Theatre" title="Golden Gate Theatre">
       Golden Gate Theatre
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
       San Francisco
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Ahmanson_Theatre" title="Ahmanson Theatre">
       Ahmanson Theatre
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">
       Los Angeles
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canon_Theatre" title="Canon Theatre">
       Canon Theatre
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">
       Toronto
      </a>
      , the San Diego Civic Theatre in
      <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">
       San Diego
      </a>
      , the Tucson Music Hall in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tucson" title="Tucson">
       Tucson
      </a>
      , and played its final performances at the Segerstrom Hall in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Costa_Mesa" title="Costa Mesa">
       Costa Mesa
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      where it closed on 18 October 2009.
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Second National tour (2010)
      </dt>
     </dl>
     <p>
      A Second North American tour launched on 24 September 2010 from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterbury,_CT" title="Waterbury, CT">
       Waterbury, CT
      </a>
      and ended 26 June 2011 in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas,_TX" title="Dallas, TX">
       Dallas, TX
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Leading the tour was a non-equity cast, however it used the same sets and costumes as the First National tour. The cast included Steve McCoy as King Arthur, Caroline Bowman as the Lady of the Lake, Adam Grabau as Lancelot, Jacob L. Smith as Galahad, Matt Ban as Sir Bedevere/Dennis's Mother, Glenn Giron as Patsy, Martin Glyer as Robin, Thomas DeMarcus as The Historian, and John Garry as Not Dead Fred/Prince Herbert. Other cast members include Stephen Cerf, Jennifer Cordiner, Carl Draper, William Harrell, Melissa Denise Lopez, Shaun Patrick Moe, Linda Neel, Jeffrey Shankle, Keleen Snowgren, Tara Sweeney, Michael Warrell, Jessica Wockenfuss, Matthew Alexander, and Jenny Holahan. The tour restarted later that year and ran through 2012.
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Third National tour (2013)
      </dt>
     </dl>
     <p>
      A third North American tour was undertaken in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="West_End_and_UK_tour">
       West End and UK tour
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: West End and UK tour">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palace_theatre_spamalot.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Palace_theatre_spamalot.JPG/200px-Palace_theatre_spamalot.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Palace_theatre_spamalot.JPG/300px-Palace_theatre_spamalot.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Palace_theatre_spamalot.JPG/400px-Palace_theatre_spamalot.JPG 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palace_theatre_spamalot.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Spamalot showing at the Palace Theatre in October 2008.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A
      <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
       London
      </a>
      production opened at the
      <a href="/wiki/Palace_Theatre,_London" title="Palace Theatre, London">
       Palace Theatre
      </a>
      on
      <a href="/wiki/Shaftesbury_Avenue" title="Shaftesbury Avenue">
       Shaftesbury Avenue
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">
       West End
      </a>
      , commencing 30 September 2006 (London premiere 17 October) with tickets on sale booking to November 2008. Curry reprised his Broadway role as King Arthur until December, with Beale taking over from January. Sieber also reprised his rle as Sir Galahad before leaving in early 2007, replaced by Graham McDuff.
      <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Waddingham" title="Hannah Waddingham">
       Hannah Waddingham
      </a>
      was cast as the Lady of the Lake,
      <a href="/wiki/Tom_Goodman-Hill" title="Tom Goodman-Hill">
       Tom Goodman-Hill
      </a>
      as Sir Lancelot,
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hands" title="Robert Hands">
       Robert Hands
      </a>
      as Sir Robin, David Birell as Patsy, Tony Timberlake as Sir Bedevere and Darren Southworth as Prince Herbert. Notable cast replacements have included
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Davison" title="Peter Davison">
       Peter Davison
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bill_Ward_(actor)" title="Bill Ward (actor)">
       Bill Ward
      </a>
      in 2007 and, briefly,
      <a href="/wiki/Marin_Mazzie" title="Marin Mazzie">
       Marin Mazzie
      </a>
      , in early 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Sanjeev_Bhaskar" title="Sanjeev Bhaskar">
       Sanjeev Bhaskar
      </a>
      took over from
      <a href="/wiki/Alan_Dale" title="Alan Dale">
       Alan Dale
      </a>
      as the last King Arthur (23 June 2008 onwards). The London production closed on 3 January 2009.
     </p>
     <p>
      A UK tour scheduled for later in 2009 was initially postponed, the producers commenting "Due to unforeseen circumstances the UK Tour of Spamalot will not be taking place as scheduled in 2009",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but eventually started at the
      <a href="/wiki/New_Wimbledon_Theatre" title="New Wimbledon Theatre">
       New Wimbledon Theatre
      </a>
      on 29 May  5 June 2010 and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nottingham_Theatre_Royal" title="Nottingham Theatre Royal">
       Nottingham Theatre Royal
      </a>
      on 712 June 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The tour is scheduled to run until June 2011 at the Mayflower Theatre in
      <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">
       Southampton
      </a>
      . The production travelled to Trieste's Politeama Rossetti marking on 24 May 2011 the official opening of the show in Italy.
     </p>
     <p>
      Phill Jupitus
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      played King Arthur in the UK tour.
      <a href="/wiki/Todd_Carty" title="Todd Carty">
       Todd Carty
      </a>
      played
      <a href="/wiki/Patsy" title="Patsy">
       Patsy
      </a>
      , assistant to
      <a href="/wiki/King_Arthur" title="King Arthur">
       King Arthur
      </a>
      for the duration of the tour.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Phil Jupitus finished on the tour after performing at
      <a href="/wiki/Wycombe_Swan" title="Wycombe Swan">
       Wycombe Swan
      </a>
      theatre.
      <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Brigstocke" title="Marcus Brigstocke">
       Marcus Brigstocke
      </a>
      made his musical theatre debut as King Arthur following Jupitus' departure.
      <a href="/wiki/Jodie_Prenger" title="Jodie Prenger">
       Jodie Prenger
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hayley_Tamaddon" title="Hayley Tamaddon">
       Hayley Tamaddon
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Amy_Nuttall" title="Amy Nuttall">
       Amy Nuttall
      </a>
      shared the role of The Lady of the Lake. The tour also featured Simon Lipkin as Sir Galahad, Graham McDuff as Sir Lancelot, David Lingham as Prince Herbert, Samuel Holmes as Sir Robin, and Robin Armstrong as Sir Bedevere.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The UK tour also featured for the first time a re-working of the song "You won't succeed on Broadway" which has been renamed "You won't succeed in showbiz". The theme of the song has been changed from poking fun at the need for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">
       Jewish
      </a>
      input into Broadway productions and instead mocks the cross over of celebrities in musicals and reality television competitions such as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" title="The X Factor (UK)">
       X Factor
      </a>
      . It notably pokes fun at reality TV celebrities including
      <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">
       Simon Cowell
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cheryl_Cole" title="Cheryl Cole">
       Cheryl Cole
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Susan_Boyle" title="Susan Boyle">
       Susan Boyle
      </a>
      (who is shot by Sir Robin when she begins to sing).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The show was revived on the West End for seven weeks during the summer of 2012 and played for a limited time at the
      <a href="/wiki/Harold_Pinter_Theatre" title="Harold Pinter Theatre">
       Harold Pinter Theatre
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (using some of the costumes, sets, and actors from the UK Tour).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Brigstocke" title="Marcus Brigstocke">
       Marcus Brigstocke
      </a>
      (who had appeared on the tour) shared the role of King Arthur with
      <a href="/wiki/Jon_Culshaw" title="Jon Culshaw">
       Jon Culshaw
      </a>
      for those seven weeks. The production moved to the
      <a href="/wiki/Playhouse_Theatre" title="Playhouse Theatre">
       Playhouse Theatre
      </a>
      on 14 November 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The show announced in January it would close on 22 February 2014,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but was later extended
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and will now close on 12 April 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During 2013 a number of celebrities each played the part of God for a week in aid of charity, including
      <a href="/wiki/Gary_Lineker" title="Gary Lineker">
       Gary Lineker
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Windsor" title="Barbara Windsor">
       Barbara Windsor
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">
       Brian May
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Palin" title="Michael Palin">
       Michael Palin
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      UK Casts:

       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>

        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Las_Vegas">
       Las Vegas
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Las Vegas">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A production of the musical began
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">
       Las Vegas, Nevada
      </a>
      previewed on 8 March 2007 and opened on 31 March 2007 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Wynn_Las_Vegas" title="Wynn Las Vegas">
       Wynn Las Vegas
      </a>
      in the newly renamed Grail Theater (formerly the Broadway Theater, which housed a production of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Avenue_Q" title="Avenue Q">
        Avenue Q
       </a>
      </i>
      ), with an extended balcony to allow for more seating, and a redesigned interior. As with other Las Vegas transfers of Broadway musicals, including
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (1986 musical)">
        The Phantom of the Opera
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      was condensed to run in ninety minutes without an intermission. Among the cuts were the song "All For One", most of the song "Run Away", the Knights of Ni receiving their shrubbery, and the "Make sure he doesn't leave" scene with Prince Herbert's guards.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Actor
      <a href="/wiki/John_O%27Hurley" title="John O'Hurley">
       John O'Hurley
      </a>
      starred as King Arthur.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Due to the Las Vegas production, the North American touring company would not perform in
      <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
       California
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">
       Arizona
      </a>
      , or
      <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">
       Nevada
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wynnwoos_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wynnwoos-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition to O'Hurley, the cast included Nikki Crawford as Lady of the Lake, Edward Staudenmayer as Galahad,
      <a href="/wiki/J_Anthony_Crane" title="J Anthony Crane">
       J Anthony Crane
      </a>
      as Lancelot, Justin Brill as Patsy, and Harry Bouvy as Robin, with
      <a href="/wiki/Reva_Rice" title="Reva Rice">
       Reva Rice
      </a>
      as the standby Lady of the Lake.
     </p>
     <p>
      Although initially contracted to run for up to ten years
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wynnwoos_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-wynnwoos-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      its final performance was on 18 July 2008. The Las Vegas production closed to make way for
      <a href="/wiki/Danny_Gans" title="Danny Gans">
       Danny Gans
      </a>
      ' move from
      <a href="/wiki/The_Mirage" title="The Mirage">
       The Mirage
      </a>
      casino hotel; the theater was renamed the Encore Theater and integrated into the newer
      <a href="/wiki/Encore_Las_Vegas" title="Encore Las Vegas">
       Encore Las Vegas
      </a>
      resort.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATB122208_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-LATB122208-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Danny Gans died
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      unexpectedly on 1 May 2009.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">
       Australia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Australia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A new
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian" title="Australian">
       Australian
      </a>
      production started in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melbourne,_Australia" title="Melbourne, Australia">
       Melbourne
      </a>
      in November 2007 at
      <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Theatre,_Melbourne" title="Her Majesty's Theatre, Melbourne">
       Her Majesty's Theatre
      </a>
      , with the official premiere on 1 December. The cast featured
      <a href="/wiki/Bille_Brown" title="Bille Brown">
       Bille Brown
      </a>
      as King Arthur and Lucinda Shaw as the Lady of the Lake,
      <a href="/wiki/Ben_Lewis_(actor)" title="Ben Lewis (actor)">
       Ben Lewis
      </a>
      as Sir Galahad,
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hall" title="Stephen Hall">
       Stephen Hall
      </a>
      as Sir Lancelot, Derek Metzger as Patsy, Jason Langley as Sir Robin and
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_Conaghan" title="Mark Conaghan">
       Mark Conaghan
      </a>
      as Prince Herbert, with Christina O'Neill as the standby Lady of the Lake.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Australian production closed on 5 April 2008, due to lack of ticket sales and no tour followed.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Australian non-professional premiere season of
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      was presented by Phoenix Ensemble at the Pavilion Theatre in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beenleigh" title="Beenleigh">
       Beenleigh
      </a>
      and the Logan Entertainment Centre from 20 March to 25 April 2009 for 16 performances. This production won several awards at the Gold Coast Theatre Awards including Best Musical Direction (Casey Chadwick and Ben Murray), Best Set Design (Tracey and Luke Hutley, Doug McClean) and Best Actress in a Leading Role in a Musical (Natasha York). It was also nominated for Best Costumes (Glynis Aubrey) and Best Choreography (Scott Hollingsworth).
     </p>
     <p>
      The Gold Coast premiere season of
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      opened at the Spotlight Theatre,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benowa" title="Benowa">
       Benowa
      </a>
      on 24 July 2009 for a four-week run. The Sydney premiere of
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      was held on 9 October 2009 by The Regals Musical Society.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In Adelaide, a new production of
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      opened on 12 March 2010 at the Shedley Theatre.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Brisbane premiere of
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      opened 23 April 2010 at the Schonell Theatre. It was also the inaugural production of Queensland's latest new theatre company 'Blue Fish Theatrical Productions.'
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      featured a cast of Brisbane performers  Gary Rose as King Arthur, Bradley McCaw as Patsy, Tony Campbell as Sir Robin, Chris Kellett as Sir Lancelot, Lionel Theunissen as Sir Galahad, Steve Norris as Sir Bedevere (also played by Jason Lawson in a special guest appearance), Tye Shepherd as Finland Mayor/Not Dead Fred/Prince Herbet/Robin's Minstrel and Brother Maynard and Ruth Bridgstock as the Lady of the Lake.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Canberra premiere was in May 2010 at the ANU Arts Centre by SUPA Productions. Max Gambale as King Arthur, Louiza Blomfield as the Lady of the Lake, Will Huang as Patsy, Joseph McGrail-Bateup as Sir Robin, Patrick J Gallagher as Mrs Galahad, Dave Smith as Galahad and Michael Jordan as Lancelot. Director  Ron Dowd
     </p>
     <p>
      The show had its Tasmanian premiere in October 2010 at the Theatre Royal, Hobart produced by the Tasmanian Theatre Unit Trust.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Empire Theatre in Toowoomba, Australia's largest regional theatre, presented
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      in October 2010.
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      was presented in Perth in November 2010, by Playlovers in Hackett Hall, Floreat.
     </p>
     <p>
      In October 2014,
      <a href="/wiki/Harvest_Rain_Theatre_Company" title="Harvest Rain Theatre Company">
       Harvest Rain Theatre Company
      </a>
      under the direction of producer
      <a href="/wiki/Tim_O%27Connor_(actor/director)" title="Tim O'Connor (actor/director)">
       Tim O'Connor
      </a>
      staged a production of Spamalot with a cast list including
      <a href="/wiki/Jon_English" title="Jon English">
       Jon English
      </a>
      as King Arthur,
      <a href="/wiki/Simon_Gallaher" title="Simon Gallaher">
       Simon Gallaher
      </a>
      as Patsy,
      <a href="/wiki/Julie_Anthony_(singer)" title="Julie Anthony (singer)">
       Julie Anthony
      </a>
      as The Lady Of The Lake, and
      <a href="/wiki/Frank_Woodley" title="Frank Woodley">
       Frank Woodley
      </a>
      as Sir Robin. The production was presented in The Concert Hall at QPAC in Brisbane.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">
       New Zealand
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: New Zealand">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The New Zealand premiere was staged at the Globe Theatre
      <a href="/wiki/Palmerston_North" title="Palmerston North">
       Palmerston North
      </a>
      for a four-week season in November/December 2009. Hillcrest High School in Hamilton, did the second performance of Spamalot in March 2010 whilst the South Island premiere was performed by
      <a href="/wiki/Bayfield_High_School,_Dunedin" title="Bayfield High School, Dunedin">
       Bayfield High School
      </a>
      at The Mayfair Theatre, Dunedin on 1922 May 2010. Newlands College in Wellington performed a production of Spamalot in Jun 2014. Saint Kentigern College performed Spamalot as the musical production in March of 2015. At the end of June 2015, Spamalot will be performed in Tauranga, in a joined production by
      <a href="/wiki/Tauranga_Boys%27_College" title="Tauranga Boys' College">
       Tauranga Boys' College
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tauranga_Girls%27_College" title="Tauranga Girls' College">
       Tauranga Girls' College
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">
       Spain
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Spain">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The first translated production, in
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
       Spanish
      </a>
      , opened at Teatre Victoria,
      <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
       Barcelona
      </a>
      on 9 September 2008 and closed on 10 May 2009. Directed by Catalan Comedy Group
      <a href="/wiki/Tricicle" title="Tricicle">
       Tricicle
      </a>
      and choreographed by Francesc Abs, the cast included
      <a href="/wiki/Jordi_Bosch" title="Jordi Bosch">
       Jordi Bosch
      </a>
      as King Arthur,
      <a href="/wiki/Marta_Ribera" title="Marta Ribera">
       Marta Ribera
      </a>
      as the Lady of the Lake, Sergi Albert as Sir Galahad (later replaced by Edu Soto), Fernando Gil as Sir Lancelot, Julin Fontalvo as Patsy, Xavi Duch as Sir Robin, Josep M. Gimeno as Sir Bedevere and Jess Garca as Prince Herbert, with Sara Prez as the standby Lady of the Lake. The Original Barcelona Cast Recording was released on December 2008.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 10 September 2009
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the production was transferred to Teatro Lope de Vega,
      <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
       Madrid
      </a>
      with some changes in the cast: Dulcinea Jurez as the Lady of the Lake, Ignasi Vidal as Sir Galahad, Vctor Ullate Roche as Sir Robin and Lorena Calero as the standby Lady of the Lake. The show finally closed on 28 February 2010, after more than 450 performances.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">
       Germany
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Germany">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A
      <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
       German
      </a>
      production premiered in January 2009 at the Musical Dome in
      <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">
       Cologne
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ksta-1217541660953_38-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ksta-1217541660953-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The last performance was held on 13 September 2009 at the venue.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">
       Hungary
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hungary">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The Hungarian production has started on September 2009 at the Madch Theatre in Budapest.
      <a class="external text" href="http://madachszinhaz.hu/Ea_Madach/Spamalot/Spamalot.php" rel="nofollow">
       Further information
      </a>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">
       Sweden
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sweden">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The Swedish production opened on the Malm Njesteater in
      <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6" title="Malm">
       Malm
      </a>
      on 24 September 2010, and moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Oscarsteatern" title="Oscarsteatern">
       Oscarsteatern
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">
       Stockholm
      </a>
      one year later and opened on 15 September 2011 where it played through 29 April 2012.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Nina_S%C3%B6derquist" title="Nina Sderquist">
       Nina Sderquist
      </a>
      , who starred as the last Lady of the Lake in the West End production was thought to reprise her role in the Swedish production, but when she became pregnant she was replaced by Anki Albertsson. However, Sderquist returned to the show when it moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">
       Stockholm
      </a>
      in fall 2011.
     </p>
     <p>
      The show parodied both
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (1986 musical)">
        The Phantom of the Opera
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Singin%27_in_the_Rain_(musical)" title="Singin' in the Rain (musical)">
        Singin' in the Rain
       </a>
      </i>
      through scenography and choreography. Both shows ran earlier at the same theatre to critical acclaim.
     </p>
     <p>
      The show was performed in Swedish with translation by Adde Malmberg, who played Sir Lancelot in the show in both Malm and Stockholm. Kim Sulocki, who played Patsy in the Swedish show will reprise his rle in Norwegian in
      <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">
       Oslo
      </a>
      2012.
     </p>

      </span>

     <p>
      The Belgian production will be directed by Belgian actor and director Stany Crets.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
