     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Czech_Republic">
       Czech Republic
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Czech Republic">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The premiere of Czech production took place on 6 March 2010 in the
      <a href="/wiki/J._K._Tyl_Theatre" title="J. K. Tyl Theatre">
       J. K. Tyl Theatre
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Plze%C5%88" title="Plze">
       Pilsen
      </a>
      . The play achieved a great success. It is a completely translated version by Adam Novk and directed by Roman Meluzn.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The premiere in
      <a href="/wiki/Liberec" title="Liberec">
       Liberec
      </a>
      will open on 25 April 2014 directed by Petr Palou.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

      <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Fran%C3%A7ois_Martin-Laval" title="Pierre-Franois Martin-Laval">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">
       Poland
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Poland">
        edit
       </a>

       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Since 25 September 2010 "Spamalot" is played at the music theatre in Gdynia, Poland, directed by Maciej Korwin. The premire took place on 2 October 2010.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">
       Canada
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Canada">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Mecca Productions of Brandon, Manitoba staged their production of Spamalot 1821 November 2010. This marks the first time a non-professional company has performed the show in Canada. The production stars James Comrie as King Arthur, Lisa Vasconcelos as The Lady of the Lake, Chris Isaak as Sir Dennis Galahad, Bob Brereton as Patsy, Dylan Woodcock as Sir Robin, Brody Harms as Sir Lancelot, and John Szabo as Sir Bedevere.
     </p>
     <p>
      Ontario's premiere amateur performance of 'SPAMalot' was staged in Windsor, Ontario at the Chrysler Centre of the Performing Arts in November 2012 through Windsor Light Music Theatre as their 126th successive major musical production. Directed by John Whatley, the production relied heavily on English dialect coaching by Eryl Child making sure it was true to the beloved Python films and gags. The "new musical lovingly ripped off from the motion picture" featured Ryan Turgeon as King Arthur, Lia Khan as the Lady of the Lake, Matthew Steckle as Sir Galahad, Christopher Hickman as Patsy, Jakob Skrzypa as Sir Robin, Jim Reid as Sir Lancelot, and Christopher Fazekas as Sir Bedevere.
     </p>
     <p>
      Spamalot was produced in Calgary by Front Row Centre Players as part of their 201213 season: shows were 1126 January at the Pumphouse Theatres.
     </p>
     <p>
      Spamalot was produced by the
      <a href="/wiki/Citadel_Theatre" title="Citadel Theatre">
       Citadel Theatre
      </a>
      in Edmonton, Alberta as part of their 20122013 season. It ran 20 April  19 May 2013
     </p>
     <p>
      Spamalot was produced by VOS (Victorian Operetta Society) in Cobourg, Ontario in April 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Spamalot was produced by Hatrix Theatre Company and Danceworks in Lethbridge, Alberta, April 15-20, 2013 at the Yates Memorial Theatre.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The 2013 Lawyer Show in Vancouver, BC, in combination with
      <a href="/wiki/Touchstone_Theatre" title="Touchstone Theatre">
       Touchstone Theatre
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Carousel_Theatre" title="Carousel Theatre">
       Carousel Theatre
      </a>
      will be Spamalot. The show ran 14 May 2013 at Waterfront Theatre.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Spamalot was produced by
      <a href="/wiki/Drayton_Entertainment" title="Drayton Entertainment">
       Drayton Entertainment
      </a>
      at the St. Jacobs Country Playhouse and Huron Country Playhouse in the summer of 2013. Notable stars include Victor A. Young as King Arthur, Nick Settimi as Patsy, Kristen Peace as The Lady of the Lake, Stephen Patterson as Sir Gallahad and Thomas Alderson as Prince Herbert. The production is Directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Alex_Mustakas" title="Alex Mustakas">
       Alex Mustakas
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Spamalot was produced by Schmooze Productions in Nanaimo, British Columbia as part of the 2013 season from 14 November to 7 December at the Nanaimo Centre Stage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Spamalot was produced by
      <a href="/wiki/Orpheus_Musical_Theatre_Society" title="Orpheus Musical Theatre Society">
       Orpheus Musical Theatre Society
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and ran from 7 to 16 March 2014 at
      <a href="/wiki/Centrepointe_Theatre" title="Centrepointe Theatre">
       Centrepointe Theatre
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The show was produced by Medicine Hat Musical Theatre in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medicine_Hat,_Alberta" title="Medicine Hat, Alberta">
       Medicine Hat, Alberta
      </a>
      from 21-23 and 27-29 March 2014. The cast included Richard Grafton as King Arthur, Bob Donaldson as Patsy, Shannon Clish Welsh as The Lady of the Lake, Pat Weisgerber as Lancelot, Doug Frelick as Galahad, Rob Olson as Robin and Stephen Philpott as Bedevere.
     </p>
     <p>
      Spamalot was produced by the
      <a href="/wiki/Arts_Club_Theatre_Company" title="Arts Club Theatre Company">
       Arts Club Theatre Company
      </a>
      in Vancouver. The show runs from 8 May to 29 June at the
      <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Industrial_Alliance_Stage" title="Stanley Industrial Alliance Stage">
       Stanley Industrial Alliance Stage
      </a>
      . The cast includes Andrew Cownden, Josh Epstein, Jay Hindle, Terra C. MacLeod, David Marr, Ashley OConnell, Scott Perrie and Jonathan Winsby.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Spamalot was produced by Stage West Theatre in Calgary, AB in spring 2015. The show ran from April 16 - June 21, 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">

       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Ireland">

     <p>

      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">

      </a>
      .

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">
       Italy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Italy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In May 2011, the original UK touring production played at
      <a href="/wiki/Politeama_Rossetti" title="Politeama Rossetti">
       Politeama Rossetti
      </a>
      in Trieste. Eric Idle attended the opening night on 24 May.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">
       Netherlands
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Netherlands">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In April 2011 a Dutch touring version opened, starring comedians Paul Groot and Owen Schumacher. The entire cast also appeared in character on Dutch TV in a Python/Spamalot tribute: "Help, mijn man is ridder!" (Help! My husband is a knight!).
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">
       Mexico
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Mexico">

       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The premiere for the Mexican version of the show was on July 2011 in
      <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">
       Mexico City
      </a>
      . The show ran for over 500 performances across the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">
       Japan
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Japan">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The Japanese version played at two theaters in January and February 2012. The musical ran from 9 to 22 January 2012, at the Akasaka Blitz theater in Tokyo. It then played at the Morinomiya Piloti Hall in Osaka from 2 February to February to 6 February. The musical stars Yusuke Santamaria as King Arthur, Mao Ayabuki as The Lady of The Lake, Narushi Ikeda as Sir Lancelot, Shigeyuki Totsugi as Sir Robin, Kento Kaku as Sir Dennis Galahad, Sarutoki Minagawa as Sir Bedevere, and Magy as Patsy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From 16 February to 1 March 2015 the show will be performed at Akasaka ACT Theater, Tokyo.
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_by_Monty_Python_members">
       Reactions by Monty Python members
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Reactions by Monty Python members">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <table class="rquote floatright" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:right; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">
      <tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
       <td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">
        
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0 10px;">
        "I'm making them money, and the ungrateful bastards never thank me. Who gave them a million dollars each for 'Spamalot'?"
       </td>
       <td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">
        
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px;">
        <p style="font-size:smaller; line-height:1em; text-align:right">
         Eric Idle
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
          <a href="#cite_note-54">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           54
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </p>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      The show has had mixed reactions from Idle's former colleagues in Monty Python.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Terry_Gilliam" title="Terry Gilliam">
       Terry Gilliam
      </a>
      , in an audio interview,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tgint_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-tgint-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      describes it as "Python-lite". He later told the BBC News, "It helps with the pension fund, and it helps keep Python alive. As much as we'd like to pull the plug on the whole thing it carries on  it's got a life of its own."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Terry_Jones" title="Terry Jones">
       Terry Jones
      </a>
       who co-directed the original film with Gilliam  expressed his opinions forthrightly in May 2005: "
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      is utterly pointless. It's full of airRegurgitating Python is not high on my list of priorities."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, when asked whether he liked
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      during an interview with
      <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Daniel" title="Dennis Daniel">
       Dennis Daniel
      </a>
      on 98.5
      <a href="/wiki/WBON" title="WBON">
       WBON
      </a>
      -FM "The BONE" on Long Island shortly after the musical's opening on Broadway, Jones said, "Well, I thought it was terrific good fun. Its great to see the audience loving it. I suppose I had reservations as far aswellthe idea of doing scenes from a film on stage. I just dont get the point of it. They do them terribly wellI mean, they really are goodbut I just quite dont understand what thats about. It isnt really 'Python.' It is very much
      <a href="/wiki/Eric_Idle" title="Eric Idle">
       Eric
      </a>
      ." Jones went on to say, "...I think the best parts of the musical are the new things. For instance, when they do the Andrew Lloyd Webber take-off and this girl comes in and sings 'Whatever Happened to My Part' since she hasnt appeared since the opening number and shes really furious! That is one of the great moments where the show really comes alive for me."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In an Oct. 2006 interview,
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Palin" title="Michael Palin">
       Michael Palin
      </a>
      said, "Were all hugely delighted that
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      is doing so well. Because were all beneficiaries! Its a great show. Its not Python as we would have written it. But then, none of us would get together and write a Python stage show. Eric eventually ran out of patience and said, Well, Ill do it myself then. He sent us bits and songs and all that and we said, Yeah, thats all right, have a go. But its success is so enormous that it took us all by surprise, including Eric, and now were just proud to be associated with it, rather pathetically."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      When asked by a
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Review-Journal" title="Las Vegas Review-Journal">
        Las Vegas Review-Journal
       </a>
      </i>
      reporter in 2008 if he had to be persuaded to provide the recorded voice of God in the musical,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Cleese" title="John Cleese">
       John Cleese
      </a>
      said, "Yeah, thats right. And in the end I think
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      turned out splendidly. Its had a tremendous run. I defy anyone to go and not have a really fun evening. Its the silliest thing Ive ever seen and I think Eric did a great job."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception_and_box-office">
       Critical reception and box-office
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Critical reception and box-office">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The original production has been both a financial and critical success.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">
        Variety
       </a>
      </i>
      reported advance ticket sales of $18 million, with ticket prices ranging from $36 to $179. The advance made Broadway box office history.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The show proved to be an early success when moving to London's West End. After high advance ticket sales the show's run was extended by four weeks, four months before the run commenced.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The play makes many references to the film and other material in the Python
      <a href="/wiki/Canon_(fiction)" title="Canon (fiction)">
       canon
      </a>
      , including a line from "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Lumberjack_Song" title="The Lumberjack Song">
       The Lumberjack Song
      </a>
      ", nods to "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Ministry_of_Silly_Walks" title="The Ministry of Silly Walks">
       Ministry of Silly Walks
      </a>
      ", the "Election Night Special" and "
      <a href="/wiki/Dead_Parrot_sketch" title="Dead Parrot sketch">
       Dead Parrot sketch
      </a>
      " routines, a
      <a href="/wiki/Bar_(music)" title="Bar (music)">
       bar
      </a>
      from "
      <a href="/wiki/Spam_(Monty_Python)" title="Spam (Monty Python)">
       Spam
      </a>
      " worked into "Knights of the Round Table", a rendition of the song "
      <a href="/wiki/Always_Look_on_the_Bright_Side_of_Life" title="Always Look on the Bright Side of Life">
       Always Look on the Bright Side of Life
      </a>
      " from the film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_Life_of_Brian" title="Monty Python's Life of Brian">
        Monty Python's Life of Brian
       </a>
      </i>
      (1979), and the "Fisch Schlapping Song" which is a reference to both "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Fish-Slapping_Dance" title="The Fish-Slapping Dance">
       The Fish-Slapping Dance
      </a>
      " and the song "
      <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_Contractual_Obligation_Album" title="Monty Python's Contractual Obligation Album">
       Finland
      </a>
      ". Another reference is actually part of the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Playbill" title="Playbill">
        Playbill
       </a>
      </i>
      of the show; there are several gag pages about a musical entitled "Dik Od Triaanenen Fol (Finns Ain't What They Used To Be)". This gag programme was written by Palin, and echoes the
      <i>
       faux
      </i>
      -Swedish subtitles in the credits of the original
      <i>
       Grail
      </i>
      Python film.
     </p>
     <p>
      Broadway musical fans appreciate its references to other musicals and musical theatre in general, such as: "The Song That Goes Like This" (a spoof of
      <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lloyd_Webber" title="Andrew Lloyd Webber">
       Andrew Lloyd Webber
      </a>
      productions and many other Broadway
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_ballad" title="Power ballad">
       power ballads
      </a>
      ); the knights doing a dance reminiscent of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Fiddler_on_the_Roof" title="Fiddler on the Roof">
        Fiddler on the Roof
       </a>
      </i>
      , and another reminiscent of
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Side_Story_(musical)" title="West Side Story (musical)">
        West Side Story
       </a>
      </i>
      (including the music); Sir Lancelot's mimicking of
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Allen_(musician)" title="Peter Allen (musician)">
       Peter Allen
      </a>
      in "His Name Is Lancelot"; the character of Sir Not Appearing in This Show being
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Man_of_La_Mancha" title="Man of La Mancha">
        Man of La Mancha
       </a>
       '
      </i>
      s
      <a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">
       Don Quixote
      </a>
      ; a member of the French "army" dressed as Eponine from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Les_Mis%C3%A9rables_(musical)" title="Les Misrables (musical)">
        Les Misrables
       </a>
      </i>
      ; and a line pulled from "Another Hundred People" from
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sondheim" title="Stephen Sondheim">
       Stephen Sondheim
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Company_(musical)" title="Company (musical)">
        Company
       </a>
      </i>
      by the "damsel" Herbert. The song "You Won't Succeed (On Broadway)" also parodies
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Producers_(musical)" title="The Producers (musical)">
        The Producers
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Yentl" title="Yentl">
        Yentl
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The show has not escaped criticism. In
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">
        Slate
       </a>
      </i>
      , Sam Anderson wrote, "Python was formed in reaction to exactly the kind of lazy comedy represented by
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
       what Michael Palin once described as the 'easy, catch-phrase reaction' the members had all been forced to pander in their previous writing jobs...
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      is the gaudy climax of a long, unfunny tradition of post-Python exploitation  books, actions figures, video games  that treats the old material as a series of slogans to be referenced without doing any of the work that made the lines so original in the first place."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The West End version opened to two rave reviews. "Its a wonderful night, and I fart in the general direction of anyone who says otherwise", wrote
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_Spencer_(journalist)" title="Charles Spencer (journalist)">
       Charles Spencer
      </a>
      in the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daily_Telegraph" title="Daily Telegraph">
        Daily Telegraph
       </a>
      </i>
      (echoing a joke from the show).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph1_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-telegraph1-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to Paul Taylor in the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_(newspaper)" title="Independent (newspaper)">
        Independent
       </a>
      </i>
      , "it leaves you that high and weak with laughter, thanks not just to the Python provenance of the basic material but to the phenomenal speed, wit, cheek and showbiz knowingness of the direction, which is by the great veteran, Mike Nichols".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent1_64-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-independent1-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Billington_(critic)" title="Michael Billington (critic)">
       Michael Billington
      </a>
      in the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guardian_(newspaper)" title="Guardian (newspaper)">
        Guardian
       </a>
      </i>
      was less enthusiastic, though, stating "while I'm happy to see musicals spoofed, the show's New York origins are clearly exposed in a would-be outre number which announces "we won't succeed in show business if we don't have any Jews": a Broadway in-joke that has little purchase this side of the
      <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
       Atlantic
      </a>
      ." Billington adds, "With hand on heart, I'd much rather watch Lerner and Loewe's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Camelot_(musical)" title="Camelot (musical)">
        Camelot
       </a>
      </i>
      than Eric Idle's smart-arsed
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian1_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-guardian1-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Las Vegas production was awarded the Number 1 show of 2007 by the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Review-Journal" title="Las Vegas Review-Journal">
        Las Vegas Review-Journal
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Coconut_orchestra_world_record">
       Coconut orchestra world record
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Coconut orchestra world record">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 22 March 2006, to mark the first anniversary of the official Broadway opening, the "World's Largest Coconut Orchestra", 1,789 people clapping together half coconut shells, performed in
      <a href="/wiki/Shubert_Alley" title="Shubert Alley">
       Shubert Alley
      </a>
      , outside the theatre. The claim was officially recognised by the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_World_Records" title="Guinness Book of World Records">
        Guinness Book of World Records
       </a>
      </i>
      . This record was broken by 5,567 people in
      <a href="/wiki/Trafalgar_Square" title="Trafalgar Square">
       Trafalgar Square
      </a>
      at 7pm on 23 April 2007, led by the cast from the London production, along with Jones and Gilliam, with the coconuts used in place of the whistles in "Always Look on the Bright Side of Life". This formed part of London's
      <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Day" title="St George's Day">
       St George's Day
      </a>
      celebrations that year and was followed by a screening of
      <i>
       Monty Python and the Holy Grail
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC658187_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC658187-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other">
       Other
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Other">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SPAMALOT_bright_sign.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1042" data-file-width="665" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/SPAMALOT_bright_sign.jpg/175px-SPAMALOT_bright_sign.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/SPAMALOT_bright_sign.jpg/263px-SPAMALOT_bright_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/SPAMALOT_bright_sign.jpg/350px-SPAMALOT_bright_sign.jpg 2x" width="175"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SPAMALOT_bright_sign.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A sign at the Shubert Theatre advertising the show's
        <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Musical">
         Best Musical
        </a>
        award.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2006, the London cast of
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      performed excerpts at the
      <a href="/wiki/Royal_Variety_Performance" title="Royal Variety Performance">
       Royal Variety Performance
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      On 10 March 2007,
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      partnered with
      <a href="/wiki/HP_Sauce" title="HP Sauce">
       HP Sauce
      </a>
      (the classic British
      <a href="/wiki/Steak_sauce" title="Steak sauce">
       brown sauce
      </a>
      , now made in the
      <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
       Netherlands
      </a>
      following a contentious decision to close its factory in Britain) to produce 1,075 limited edition bottles featuring a unique
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      take on the classic HP design. The bottles were available exclusively via
      <a href="/wiki/Selfridges" title="Selfridges">
       Selfridges
      </a>
      , London and came in a presentation box with a numbered
      <a href="/wiki/Certificate_of_authenticity" title="Certificate of authenticity">
       certificate
      </a>
      . 1,075 was chosen to celebrate, absurdly, "1,075 years of the show running in London".
     </p>
     <p>
      In July 2007 it was announced that the London production would solve the problem of replacing Hannah Waddingham as the Lady of the Lake through a TV talent show in Sweden. The programme, called West End Star, which began airing on
      <a href="/wiki/TV3_(Sweden)" title="TV3 (Sweden)">
       TV3
      </a>
      on 8 December 2007, announced
      <a href="/wiki/Nina_S%C3%B6derquist" title="Nina Sderquist">
       Nina Sderquist
      </a>
      as the winner on 2 February 2008. Sderquist took up the rle of The Lady of the Lake, with a standing ovation, on 11 February 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="DVD">
       DVD
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: DVD">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Portions of the
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/Cast_recording" title="Cast recording">
       original cast recording
      </a>
      were featured (with accompanying
      <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">
       Flash animation
      </a>
      ) as a special feature in the 2006 "Extraordinarily Deluxe Two-Disc Edition" DVD re-release of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python_and_the_Holy_Grail" title="Monty Python and the Holy Grail">
        Monty Python and the Holy Grail
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">
       Awards and nominations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In the original Broadway production, Sara Ramirez sang the line, "I've no Grammy, no reward/I've no Tony Award." Ironically, the show's original cast album won the Grammy for Best Musical Theater Album in 2006 and Ramirez herself won the Tony for Best Featured Actress in 2005. The two awards led to a minor change to the song "The Diva's Lament". Initially, the line became "My Tony Award/won't keep me out of
      <a href="/wiki/Betty_Ford_Center" title="Betty Ford Center">
       Betty Ford's
      </a>
      ". When
      <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Kennedy" title="Lauren Kennedy">
       Lauren Kennedy
      </a>
      took over for
      <a href="/wiki/Sara_Ramirez" title="Sara Ramirez">
       Sara Ramirez
      </a>
      , it became "My predecessor won awards/and now she's in Betty Ford's" but was later changed to, "
      <b>
       All our
      </b>
      Tony Awards/won't keep me out of Betty Ford's."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the touring production, Pia Glenn sings "All our
      <i>
       goddamn
      </i>
      awards/won't keep me out of Betty Ford's." For a change,
      <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Waddingham" title="Hannah Waddingham">
       Hannah Waddingham
      </a>
      in the London production sings "I'm as depressed as I can be/ I've got constant
      <a href="/wiki/Premenstrual_syndrome" title="Premenstrual syndrome">
       PMT
      </a>
      ".
     </p>
     <p>
      The touring production has garnered Boston's Elliot Norton Award for Outstanding Visiting Production.
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Television">
       Television
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Television">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      A special edition of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_South_Bank_Show" title="The South Bank Show">
        The South Bank Show
       </a>
      </i>
      was a
      <a href="/wiki/Television_documentary" title="Television documentary">
       television documentary
      </a>
      on the history of
      <i>
       Spamalot
      </i>
      . It features numerous segments with Eric Idle and John Du Prez explaining the process of writing the songs, plus interviews with UK and US cast members. It included scenes from the rehearsal of the West End show, and was first broadcast on 15 October 2006.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuit">
       Lawsuit
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spamalot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Lawsuit">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In 2013 the Pythons lost a legal case to
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_Forstater" title="Mark Forstater">
       Mark Forstater
      </a>
      , the producer of
      <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python_and_the_Holy_Grail" title="Monty Python and the Holy Grail">
       Monty Python and the Holy Grail
      </a>
      , over royalties for Spamalot. He was paid 1/14 of the portion of the profits paid to the Pythons. The court ruled that he was a full Python partner and was to be paid 1/7 of the portion paid to the Pythons. They owed a combined 800,000 in legal fees and back royalties to Forstater prompting them to produce
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monty_Python_Live_(Mostly)" title="Monty Python Live (Mostly)">
       Monty Python Live (Mostly)
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-royal_70-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-royal-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

           Last July, the Pythons lost a royalties case to Mark Forstater, who produced 1975 film Monty Python And The Holy Grail. ...
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpamalot&amp;rft.atitle=John+Cleese%3A+Monty+Python+reunion+is+happening+because+of+my+%C2%A3800%2C000+legal+bill&amp;rft.date=May+23%2C+2014&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.mirror.co.uk%2Ftv%2Ftv-news%2Fjohn-cleese-monty-python-reunion-3591253&amp;rft.jtitle=Daily+Mirror&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-royal-70">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-royal_70-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/entertainment-arts-20556684" rel="nofollow">
           "Monty Python sued over Spamalot royalties"
          </a>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_Online" title="BBC News Online">
           BBC News Online
          </a>
          . 30 November 2012
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2012-11-30
           </span>
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           Mr Forstater claimed he was entitled to one-seventh of this figure, the same share enjoyed by each of the other Pythons - but was told he was only entitled to one-fourteenth, and has been paid accordingly since 2005. ...
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpamalot&amp;rft.btitle=Monty+Python+sued+over+Spamalot+royalties&amp;rft.date=30+November+2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.bbc.co.uk%2Fnews%2Fentertainment-arts-20556684&amp;rft.pub=BBC+News+Online&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-71">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-71">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation news">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/entertainment-arts-23195478" rel="nofollow">
           "Monty Python lose Spamalot court battle"
          </a>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">
           BBC News
          </a>
          . 4 July 2013
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            5 July
           </span>
           2013
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           Mark Forstater, who produced the 1975 film Monty Python And The Holy Grail, claimed he was underpaid royalties since the musical's launch in 2005. ...
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpamalot&amp;rft.btitle=Monty+Python+lose+Spamalot+court+battle&amp;rft.date=4+July+2013&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.bbc.co.uk%2Fnews%2Fentertainment-arts-23195478&amp;rft.pub=BBC+News&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
     </div>
